# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the ext_authz filter's bypass and passthrough logic. The answer includes:

## Summary of Findings

**Bypass Configuration (Per-Route):**
- `FilterConfigPerRoute` class stores the `disabled` flag from route-specific configuration
- `getPerRouteFlags()` retrieves the most specific per-route configuration
- When disabled is true, `decodeHeaders()` returns immediately without calling the authorization service

**Authorization Decision Handling:**
The `onComplete()` method handles three outcomes:
1. **OK**: Applies header mutations, modifies query parameters, and resumes request
2. **Denied**: Sends a local response with configured status code
3. **Error**: Either allows (passthrough) or denies based on `failure_mode_allow` setting

**Immediate Response Path:**
- Synchronous authorization responses are supported via the `initiating_call_` flag
- Authorization decision can be made and applied immediately without async wait
- `continueDecoding()` resumes request processing after decision

**Authorization Service Communication:**
- gRPC client: `GrpcClientImpl` with `copyOkResponseMutations()` for response handling
- HTTP client: `RawHttpClientImpl` with `SuccessResponse` struct for header matching

The answer file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with complete documentation of all relevant files, symbols, and implementation details.

This method processes synchronous (stack-based) and asynchronous authorization responses:\\n\\n1. **OK Response (lines 432-676)**: When authorization succeeds:\\n   - Applies header mutations (headers_to_set, headers_to_add, headers_to_append)\\n   - Removes headers specified in headers_to_remove\\n   - Modifies query parameters (query_parameters_to_set, query_parameters_to_remove)\\n   - Clears route cache if configured (lines 436-441)\\n   - Adds response headers for downstream (response_headers_to_add, etc.)\\n   - Calls `Filter::continueDecoding` to resume request processing\\n\\n2. **Denied Response (lines 678-737)**: When authorization is denied:\\n   - Sends a local reply with the denied status code\\n   - Includes headers specified in headers_to_set\\n   - Sets UnauthorizedExternalService response flag\\n   - Terminates request immediately\\n\\n3. **Error Response (lines 739-767)**: When authorization service fails:\\n   - If `failure_mode_allow` is true: allows request (passthrough mode) and increments failure_mode_allowed stat\\n   - If `failure_mode_allow` is false: sends local Forbidden response\\n   - Optionally adds x-envoy-auth-failure-mode-allowed header if `failure_mode_allow_header_add` is enabled\\n\\n## Immediate Response Path\\n\\nThe filter supports synchronous (stack-based) authorization responses through the `initiating_call_` flag (line 365). When `initiating_call_` is true, the `onComplete` callback may be invoked synchronously before `check()` returns, allowing the authorization decision to be made and applied immediately without waiting for async I/O.\\n\\nThe `Filter::continueDecoding` function (source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz.cc:800-808) resumes request processing after authorization:\\n- Sets `buffer_data_` to false\\n- Sets `filter_return_` to ContinueDecoding\\n- Calls `decoder_callbacks_->continueDecoding()` only if not in synchronous mode (`!initiating_call_`)\\n\\n## Authorization Service Communication\\n\\nTwo implementations handle communication with authorization services:\\n\\n1. **gRPC Implementation** (source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_impl.h/cc):\\n   - `GrpcClientImpl::check`: Sends CheckRequest to gRPC authorization service\\n   - `GrpcClientImpl::onSuccess`: Processes CheckResponse and builds the Response object\\n   - `copyOkResponseMutations`: Converts gRPC response headers into Response mutations\\n\\n2. **HTTP Implementation** (source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_impl.h/cc):\\n   - `RawHttpClientImpl::check`: Sends authorization check via HTTP\\n   - `RawHttpClientImpl::onSuccess`: Processes HTTP response headers\\n   - `SuccessResponse` struct: Matches response headers against configured matchers to determine which headers apply to upstream, downstream, or dynamic metadata\\n\\n## Response Structure\\n\\nThe `Response` struct (source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz.h:86-129) contains the authorization decision and mutations:\\n- `status`: CheckStatus (OK, Denied, or Error)\\n- Header mutations: headers_to_set, headers_to_add, headers_to_append, headers_to_remove\\n- Response mutations: response_headers_to_add, response_headers_to_set, response_headers_to_add_if_absent, response_headers_to_overwrite_if_exists\\n- Query parameter mutations: query_parameters_to_set, query_parameters_to_remove\\n- `dynamic_metadata`: Struct containing metadata from the authorization service\\n- `body` and `status_code`: Used for denied responses to send back to client\\n\\n## Network Filter\\n\\nThe network-layer ext_authz filter (source/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/ext_authz.h/cc) implements similar bypass and decision logic for TCP/network layer authorization, with the same three decision paths (OK, Denied, Error) and failure mode handling.\"\n}\n",
